For anyone wondering, smelling salts release ammonia gas. If you breathe in this gas, it irritates the insides of your nose and lungs to such an extent that it stimulates your sympathetic ("fight-or-flight") nervous system. This is an autonomous part of your nervous system that, when activated, has all sorts of arousing effects on your body, releasing adrenaline, increasing your heart rate, opening up your lungs, increasing blood flow to your skeletal muscles (while decreasing it to your digestive system), and generally preparing your body for action. For athletes, these effects may be desirable and performance-enhancing, although perhaps especially so for athletic feats that require quick bursts of action. Smelling salts have also been used to revive athletes that have been rendered unconscious (e.g. boxers), because their arousing effects counteract the fainting response.

I relate to Tom. I too was born with Autistic Spectrum Disorder. I'm on the "High Functioning" end which means that I am blessed with having more understanding of social situations, however, subtle social cues are still a problem for me because I am also visually impaired and cannot pick up on facial expressions properly. I didn't let that stop me though. I have just passed my BA Honours in Electronic Music Production and have had a somewhat successful start to my career. Just need to find a stable 9 to 5 now and I'm happy. Autism is a buzzword at the moment that people just don't understand. We work slightly differently. That's it. We aren't incompetent. We just need black and white instructions and coping mechanisms that help us grow. That is what I was given and I feel like I'm learning from it, along with my mistakes. Peace from the UK.
